Sunnah Acts of Hajj: Hadi, Eating from Hadi, and Khutbah on Yawm al-Nahr
Presents three sunnah acts: offering hadi for Mufrid, eating from voluntary hadi, and delivering khutbah on the 10th.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah acts described, identify the hadith evidence for each, and explain the permissibility of eating from different types of hadi.

Core Idea
Offering hadi for Mufrid, eating from voluntary/tamattu'/qiran hadi, and delivering the third khutbah are sunnah acts proven by the Prophet's practice.

This lesson combines three distinct sunnah acts related to the days of Hajj. The first concerns offering a sacrificial animal for the one performing Hajj Ifrad. The second clarifies from which types of hadi the pilgrim may eat. The third establishes the sunnah of delivering a khutbah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. Each ruling is grounded in authentic hadith, demonstrating how the Prophet's actions become legal precedents in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the Arabic text carefully. It lists three separate sunnah acts: (1) offering hadi for the Mufrid, (2) eating from the hadi of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran, and (3) delivering a khutbah on the Day of Nahr. Note that each is introduced with 'من السنة' (from the sunnah).
The term 'hadi' refers to a sacrificial animal offered in the Haram during Hajj/Umrah.
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
The commentary cites two main hadiths: the long hadith of Jabir (Muslim, Abu Dawud) for rulings 1 and 2, and the hadith of Harmas ibn Ziyad (Abu Dawud) for ruling 3. Identify which part of each hadith supports which ruling.
The hadith of Jabir shows the Prophet slaughtering 63 camels with his own hand and then eating from the meat.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
For the hadi of Mufrid and eating from hadi: the Prophet's action (fi‘l) of slaughtering and eating proves the sunnah and permissibility. For the khutbah: the Prophet's action of delivering a speech on the 10th establishes the sunnah. Explain how each act of the Prophet yields the ruling.
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's fi‘l indicates recommendation (sunnah) unless there is evidence of obligation.
4
Distinguish types of hadi
The text distinguishes between penalty hadi (jinaayaat) and other hadi. Penalty hadi is only for the poor; the slaughterer cannot eat from it. Voluntary hadi, tamattu‘ hadi, qiran hadi, and the Mufrid's hadi may be eaten by the one who offered it. Trace this distinction in the commentary.
The Prophet ate from his own hadi, so any hadi that is not a penalty or expiatory offering may be consumed by the donor.
5
Place the khutbah in context
Understand that this is the third of three sunnah khutbahs during Hajj: on the 7th (before Hajj), on the 9th at Arafah, and now on the 10th at Mina. The khutbah should teach the remaining rites of Hajj.
The timing of the khutbah is before the noon prayer (forenoon), unlike the later days when the khutbah is after zawal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستحبابا. (۱۲۷۹) ومن السنة هدى المفرد بالحج (۱۲۸۰) و الاكل منه ومن هدى التطوع والمتعة والقران فقط . (۱۲۸۱) ومن السنة الخطبة يوم النحر مثل الاولى يعلّم فيها بقيّة المناسك النحر ضحى فاما بعد ذلك فبعد زوال الشمس (ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی رمي الجمارص ۲۷۸ نمبر ۱۹۷۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دسویں تاریخ کو زوال کے بعد ہی رمی کرے، اس لئے تیرہویں تاریخ کو بھی زوال کے بعد ہی رمی کرے.
ترجمه : (۱۳۷۹) ۔ حج افراد کرنے والے کے لئے ہدی کا ذبیح کرنا بھی سنت میں سے ہے
تشریح : صرف حج کرنے والے پر ہدی واجب نہیں ہے لیکن سنت ہے۔
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے . ـ دخـلـنـا علی جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم انصرف الى المنحر فنحر ثلاثا و ستين بيده ثم اعطى عليا فنحر ما غير واشركه في هدیه - ( مسلم شریف، باب حجته النبی ص ۲۹۹ نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ را بو داؤد شریف، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۱ نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رمی کے بعد مفرد کو ہو سکے تو ذبح کرنا چاہئے

ترجمه : (۱۲۸۰) اور کھانا مفرد بالج کی ہدی سے اور نفلی صدی سے اور قرآن اور تمتع کی ہدی سے جائز ہے
تشریح : جو جانور جنایات کا ہو وہ غرباء مساکین کے لئے جائز ہے، خود ذبح کرنے والے کے لئے اس کا کھانا جائز نہیں، البتہ هدی نفلی ہدی تمتع اور قرآن کی قربانی کا گوشت خود کرنے والے کے لئے جائز ہے۔
وجه : قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله فسأل عن القوم ... ثم انصرف الى المنحر فنحر ثلثا وستين بيده ثم اعطى عليا فنحر ما غبر واشركه في هديه ثم امر من كل بدنة ببضعة فجعلت في قدر فطبخت فاكلا من لحمهما وشربا من مرقها (مسلم شريف، باب حجۃ النبی ، ص ۳۹۹، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابو داؤد شریف، باب صفۃ حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۱ نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور نے ہدی کا گوشت کھایا اس لئے نفلی ہدی، قرآن اور تمتع کی ہدی کا گوشت کھانا بہتر ہے

ترجمه : (۱۲۸۱) اور دسویں تاریخ کو پہلے خطبہ کی طرح خطبہ کہنا سنت ہے، اس میں حج کے بقیہ مناسک سکھلائے جائیں، اور یہ حج کا تیسرا خطبہ ہوگا۔
تشریح : ایک خطبہ ساتویں ذی الحجہ کو دیا، دوسرا خطبہ نویں کو عرفات میں دیا، اب تیسرا خطبہ دسویں تاریخ کو دینا سنت ہے ؟ میں حج کے وہ احکام جو باقی رہ گئے ہیں وہ بیان کرے۔
وجه : حدثني الهرماس بن زياد الباهلي قال رأيت النبى الله يخطب الناس على ناقته العضباء يوم الاضحی بمنی ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب من قال خطب یوم النحر ،ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۱۹۵۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ یوم الاضحی دسویں ذی الحجہ کو خطبہ دیا۔
From the sunnah: the hadi of the one performing Hajj Ifrad. And eating from it and from the hadi of voluntary (tatawwu'), tamattu', and qiran only. And from the sunnah: the khutbah on the Day of Nahr similar to the first, in which he teaches the remaining rites. Nahr is at forenoon; after that is after zawal. (Hadith reference). This hadith indicates that on the 10th, rami is only after zawal, and similarly on the 13th. Translation of (1379): Offering a sacrifice for the Mufrid is also from the sunnah. Explanation: Hadi is not wajib on the one performing only Hajj, but it is sunnah. Evidence: In this hadith: 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he went to the slaughtering place and slaughtered 63 with his hand, then gave to Ali who slaughtered the rest, and he made him participate in his hadi.' From this hadith, it is understood that after rami, if the Mufrid is able, he should slaughter. Translation of (1280): It is permissible to eat from the hadi of the Mufrid, from voluntary hadi, and from the hadi of tamattu' and qiran. Explanation: Animals for penalties are for the poor; the slaughterer may not eat from them. However, from voluntary, tamattu', and qiran hadi, the slaughterer may eat. Evidence: The hadith of Jabir: 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... Then he went to the slaughtering place and slaughtered 63 with his hand, then gave to Ali who slaughtered the rest and made him participate in his hadi. Then he ordered from each camel a piece, put in a pot, and cooked, and they both ate from the meat and drank from the broth.' From this, it is understood that the Prophet ate from the hadi, so eating from voluntary, qiran, and tamattu' hadi is better. Translation of (1281): It is sunnah to deliver a khutbah on the 10th similar to the first, teaching the remaining rites. This is the third khutbah. Explanation: One khutbah on 7th Dhul Hijjah, second on 9th at Arafat, now the third on the 10th is sunnah. He explains the remaining rulings of Hajj. Evidence: Harmas ibn Ziyad al-Bahili said: 'I saw the Prophet of Allah delivering a khutbah to the people on his she-camel al-Adba' on the Day of Adha at Mina.' This hadith indicates that the Prophet gave a khutbah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This lesson covers three separate sunnah acts of Hajj, each with its own proof. First, offering a hadi (sacrificial animal) for the Haji Mufrid (one performing only Hajj, not Umrah) is sunnah, not wajib. The evidence is the Prophet's own action at Mina after rami. Second, it is permissible to eat from certain types of hadi: voluntary sacrifices, and the hadi of tamattu' and qiran. However, penalty animals (jinaayat) are exclusively for the poor. The Prophet himself ate from the hadi, establishing the permissibility. Third, delivering a khutbah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Nahr) is sunnah. This is the third khutbah of Hajj, following the one on the 7th and the sermon at Arafah on the 9th. The khutbah should teach the remaining rites. All three rulings are supported by authentic hadith, so they carry the weight of sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms
هدي (hadi): A sacrificial animal offered in the Haram during Hajj or Umrah.
مفرد (mufrid): One who performs Hajj only, without Umrah.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah during Hajj months and then Hajj with a break.
قران (qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah with one ihram.
خطبة (khutbah): A sermon delivered on specific occasions.
نحر (nahr): Slaughtering a camel; also refers to the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which type of hadi is it not permissible to eat from?
A) Hadi of tamattu'
B) Hadi of qiran
C) Hadi of penalty (jinaayat)
D) Voluntary hadi

Key Takeaway
Three sunnah acts of Hajj are established by the Prophet's own practice: offering hadi for Mufrid, eating from voluntary/tamattu'/qiran hadi, and delivering the khutbah on the 10th.

Leaving Mina on the 12th: The Sunnah Timing
States it is sunnah to hasten departure from Mina on the 12th before sunset.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on leaving Mina on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah and explain the consequence of remaining after sunset.

Core Idea
Leaving Mina before sunset on the 12th is sunnah; staying past sunset makes it wajib to stone on the 13th.

During Hajj, pilgrims spend the nights of Tashriq in Mina. On the 12th of Dhul Hijjah, many pilgrims intend to depart back to Makkah. The Hanafi school clarifies the recommended timing for this departure and the rule if one delays beyond sunset. This lesson explains the sunnah action and its consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaving Mina on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah. The default ruling is that it is sunnah (recommended) to hasten this departure before sunset.
Sunnah here means the Prophet ﷺ did it and encouraged it.
2
Recognize the time condition
The time critical point is sunset (ghurub al-shams). If the pilgrim leaves before sunset, they have followed the sunnah. If they remain until after sunset, a new obligation arises.
Sunset marks the end of the 12th day of Dhul Hijjah.
3
Apply the consequence of delay
If a pilgrim stays in Mina until after sunset on the 12th, it becomes wajib (necessary) to stay for the 13th and perform the stoning (rami) on that day as well.
This is because the two-day stoning period (12th and 13th) becomes linked when one reaches sunset on the 12th.
4
Synthesize the complete rule
Thus, the complete Hanafi ruling: Hastening to leave Mina before sunset on the 12th is sunnah. If you remain past sunset, you must stay for the stoning on the 13th and only then leave after stoning.
Failure to stone on the 13th when required incurs a penalty (dam).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۸۲) بارہ تاریخ کو منی سے نکلے کا ارادہ ہو تو غروب شمس سے پہلے جلدی کرنا سنت ہے ) اور اگرمنی کے قیام میں
Translation of (1382): If one intends to leave Mina on the 12th, hastening before sunset is sunnah. And if (one stays) in Mina's stay...
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This is a partial ruling about leaving Mina on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah. The text states that if a pilgrim intends to depart Mina on the 12th, it is sunnah to do so before sunset. The sentence is incomplete, but the full Hanafi position is well-known: hastening to leave before sunset is recommended, but if one remains until after sunset, then it becomes wajib to stay for the rami on the 13th as well. The missing portion likely completes this rule.

Key Terms
منی (Mina): A valley near Makkah where pilgrims spend the nights of Tashriq.
غروب شمس (ghurub al-shams): Sunset; a key time marker for Hajj rites.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what is the sunnah action for a pilgrim intending to leave Mina on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah?
A) Stay until after sunset
B) Hasten to leave before sunset
C) Leave after Fajr
D) Leave at any time

Key Takeaway
Leaving Mina before sunset on the 12th is sunnah; staying past sunset makes it wajib to stay for stoning on the 13th.

Hady for Hajj Ifrad is Sunnah
Establishes sunnah status of hady for the mufrid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hady for the mufrid and distinguish it from wajib hady for tamattu' and qiran.

Core Idea
Hady for Hajj ifrad is sunnah, not wajib; the Prophet's action shows desirability.

You already know that hady is required for tamattu' and qiran Hajj. But what if you perform only Hajj without combining Umrah? This lesson clarifies that for the mufrid, hady is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation. The source traces this ruling to the Prophet's own practice, which the Hanafi school interprets as evidence of desirability, not compulsion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the passage and find what is being ruled on (hady for mufrid) and the hukm level (sunnah). Note the explicit phrase 'من السنة هدى المفرد'.
The text categorizes it under 'من السنة', indicating it is from the sunnah, not an obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited and its source. The text quotes a portion of a hadith about the Prophet's sacrifice after ramy.
The hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud, showing the Prophet sacrificed many animals and shared with Ali.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Determine how the Prophet's action proves sunnah, not obligation. The action itself, without an accompanying command, indicates recommendation in Hanafi usul.
The imperative form is absent; the Prophet's voluntary act demonstrates desirability.
4
Distinguish from wajib hady
Contrast with tamattu' and qiran, where hady is wajib because of the Quranic verse 'فمن تمتع بالعمرة إلى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى'. For ifrad, there is no such obligation.
The hady for ifrad is purely voluntary, though highly recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲۷۹) ومن السنة هدى المفرد بالحج
ترجمه : (۱۳۷۹) ۔ حج افراد کرنے والے کے لئے ہدی کا ذبیح کرنا بھی سنت میں سے ہے
تشریح : صرف حج کرنے والے پر ہدی واجب نہیں ہے لیکن سنت ہے۔
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے . ـ دخـلـنـا علی جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم انصرف الى المنحر فنحر ثلاثا و ستين بيده ثم اعطى عليا فنحر ما غير واشركه في هدیه - ( مسلم شریف، باب حجته النبی ص ۲۹۹ نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ را بو داؤد شریف، باب صفتہ حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۱ نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رمی کے بعد مفرد کو ہو سکے تو ذبح کرنا چاہئے

Explanation: Hady is not obligatory upon the one performing only Hajj, but it is sunnah. Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of hady (sacrificial animal) for the one performing Hajj ifrad (i.e., only Hajj, not combined with Umrah). The author states that it is sunnah, not wajib. The explanation in Urdu clarifies that there is no obligation but it is recommended. The evidence is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) sacrificed numerous animals and shared with Ali, indicating that it is commendable for the mufrid to do so after the ramy of the 10th.

Key Terms
هدى (hady): The sacrificial animal offered in the Haram for Hajj or Umrah.
مفرد بالحج (mufrid bil hajj): One who performs only Hajj, without combining Umrah.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act established by the Prophet's example, not obligatory.

Hady for Hajj ifrad is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib; it is recommended but not obligatory.

Eating from Hady: What the Sacrificer May Consume
Permits eating from hady of mufrid, voluntary, tamattu', and qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between types of hady in Hanafi fiqh and state the permissibility of eating from each type, citing the prophetic practice as evidence.

Core Idea
The Prophet ate from his own hady—so voluntary and Hajj-related hady may be eaten by the sacrificer, but penalty hady cannot.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on eating from the hady (sacrificial animal) that one has offered during Hajj. The author distinguishes between two categories: hady that is voluntarily offered or given for tamattu'/qiran, and hady offered as a penalty (jinayat). The ruling is based on the Prophet's own practice, as narrated by Jabir ibn Abdullah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of hady
List the types of hady mentioned: mufrid (ifrad), tatawwu' (voluntary), tamattu', qiran, and jinayat (penalty).
The first four are permissible to eat from; jinayat is not.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each category
For mufrid, tatawwu', tamattu', and qiran: eating is permissible (mubah) and recommended. For jinayat: eating is prohibited; meat must be given to the poor.
This is the mufta bihi position from the zahir al-riwayah.
3
Locate the dalil used
The author cites the hadith of Jabir : the Prophet sacrificed 63 camels himself and shared the rest with Ali, then cooked and ate the meat and drank the broth.
Dalil type: Sunnah ahad, from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's act of eating from his own hady demonstrates permissibility and desirability for the sacrificer to eat from these types of hady.
The dalala is qat'i (definitive in meaning) though thubut is zanni (single narration).
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools may prohibit the sacrificer from eating any hady. The Hanafi school allows it for these categories, distinguishing based on the nature of the hady.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (mukhtalaf fih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲۸۰) و الاكل منه ومن هدى التطوع والمتعة والقران فقط
ترجمه : (۱۲۸۰) اور کھانا مفرد بالج کی ہدی سے اور نفلی صدی سے اور قرآن اور تمتع کی ہدی سے جائز ہے
تشریح : جو جانور جنایات کا ہو وہ غرباء مساکین کے لئے جائز ہے، خود ذبح کرنے والے کے لئے اس کا کھانا جائز نہیں، البتہ هدی نفلی ہدی تمتع اور قرآن کی قربانی کا گوشت خود کرنے والے کے لئے جائز ہے۔
وجه : قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله فسأل عن القوم ... ثم انصرف الى المنحر فنحر ثلثا وستين بيده ثم اعطى عليا فنحر ما غبر واشركه في هديه ثم امر من كل بدنة ببضعة فجعلت في قدر فطبخت فاكلا من لحمهما وشربا من مرقها (مسلم شريف، باب حجۃ النبی ، ص ۳۹۹، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ ابو داؤد شریف، باب صفۃ حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۱ نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور نے ہدی کا گوشت کھایا اس لئے نفلی ہدی، قرآن اور تمتع کی ہدی کا گوشت کھانا بہتر ہے
(1280) And eating from it and from the hady of voluntary (tatawwu'), tamattu', and qiran only. Translation: (1280) And eating from the hady of the mufrid and from voluntary charity and from the hady of qiran and tamattu' is permissible. Explanation: The animal of penalties (jinayat) is for the poor and needy; it is not permissible for the one who slaughters to eat from it. However, the meat of hady of tatawwu', tamattu', and qiran is permissible for the one who slaughters. Evidence: He said: 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah and he asked about the people... then he went to the place of sacrifice and sacrificed sixty-three with his hand, then he gave to Ali who sacrificed the rest and shared in his hady, then he ordered a piece from each camel to be placed in a pot, cooked, and they ate from the meat and drank from the broth.' (Muslim, Book of Hajj of the Prophet, p. 399 no. 2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Book of Description of the Prophet's Hajj, p. 271 no. 1905) From this it is known that the Prophet ate from the meat of hady, so eating from the meat of voluntary hady, qiran, and tamattu' is better.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This ruling addresses the permissibility of eating from the hady one has sacrificed. The author clarifies that it is permissible to eat from the hady of the mufrid, voluntary hady, and the hady of tamattu' and qiran. However, hady that is an expiation (jinayat) must be given to the poor and the sacrificer cannot eat from it. The evidence is the Prophet's action of eating from his own hady, demonstrating that it is not only permissible but commendable for the sacrificer to eat.

Key Terms
هدى التطوع (hady al-tatawwu'): Voluntary hady, not obligatory but offered optionally.
هدى المفرد (hady al-mufrid): The hady offered by the one performing only Hajj (ifrad).
جنایات (jinayat): Penalties or expiations for violating Hajj restrictions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
From which of the following types of hady is it permissible for the sacrificer to eat according to this passage?
A) Hady of penalties (jinayat)
B) Hady of tamattu'
C) Hady of ifrad only
D) Hady of qiran and tamattu' only

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the sacrificer may eat from voluntary and Hajj-related hady (mufrid, tatawwu', tamattu', qiran) but not from penalty hady (jinayat), based on the Prophet's practice.

The Sunnah Khutbah on Yawm al-Nahr
Ruling with proof from Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the khutbah on Yawm al-Nahr and identify its proof from the sunnah.

Core Idea
The khutbah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah is a sunnah of Hajj, proven by the Prophet's practice at Mina.

This passage addresses a specific sunnah act of Hajj: delivering a khutbah on Yawm al-Nahr, the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. It clarifies that this is the third of the three sunnah khutbahs of Hajj, following those on the 7th and at Arafat. The evidence is a hadith narrated by al-Harmas ibn Ziyad. Understanding this helps distinguish the Hanafi position from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? What is the hukm level (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.)? The passage states that giving a khutbah on the 10th is 'from the sunnah'.
Sunnah here refers to sunnah muakkadah, a confirmed commendable practice.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith of al-Harmas ibn Ziyad in Abu Dawud, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave a khutbah on the day of Adha at Mina.
This is a specific dalil naqli (textual evidence) from the Sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates that giving a khutbah on this day is a sunnah practice for the imam or khatib.
In Hanafi usul, a prophetic action that is not accompanied by a command indicates sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any other school disagree? The passage does not detail, but the Hanafi toolbox marks it as mukhtalaf fih. Some schools may not count this as a distinct sunnah or may have a different view.
The difference is legitimate and does not affect the validity of Hajj.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is relied upon in the Hanafi school? The mufta bihi is that the khutbah is sunnah, based on the zahir al-riwayah and the hadith.
The Hanafi position is well-supported by the evidence.

Hastening Departure from Mina Before Sunset on the 12th
Ruling on leaving Mina early vs staying until sunset on 12th

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving Mina on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah, identify the evidence from Quran and Sunnah, and explain why staying until sunset is makruh tanzih.

Core Idea
Leaving Mina before sunset on the 12th is sunnah; staying incurs no penalty but is disliked.

This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the departure (nafr) from Mina on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah. It distinguishes between the sunnah act of hastening departure before sunset and the permissible but disliked act of staying until sunset. The evidence includes the Quranic verse (2:203) and a hadith showing the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is departing from Mina on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah. The ruling: leaving before sunset is sunnah; staying until sunset is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked) with no penalty.
The text uses 'sunnah' for hastening and 'asaa' (wrongdoer) for staying, interpreted as makruh.
2
Locate the dalil
Quran 2:203 allows leaving after two days without sin; hadith of Ibn Umar shows the Prophet sometimes stayed until the 13th and performed ramy.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse explicitly permits both early and late departure, indicating no sin. The sunnah is the better practice. The hadith confirms that staying is permissible but not superior.
The Hanafi derive the disliked nature from the phrase 'asaa' (he has done wrong) in the matn.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may consider staying until sunset as permissible without dislike; Hanafi considers it makruh tanzih.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; Hanafi position is based on the wording of the matn.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
It is sunnah to hasten departure before sunset; staying is makruh. No penalty (dam) is required for staying.
This is the settled position in the zahir al-riwayah.

(۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو دن یعنی بارہویں تاریخ کو مکہ مکرمہ آئے تب بھی کوئی بات نہیں ہے، اور اگر اس کے بعد آئے تب بھی کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔

(1282) And hastening the departure (nafr) when one intends it from Mina before sunset of the twelfth day, and if he stays in it until the sun sets of the twelfth day, there is nothing upon him, but he has done wrong. Translation: (1382) On the 12th, if one intends to leave Mina, hastening before sunset is sunnah. And if he stays until sunset, there is no obligation but it is disliked. Explanation: 2 Dhul Hijjah [probably 12th], if one intends to leave Mina, leaving before sunset is sunnah, but if the sun sets, there is no harm, nothing becomes obligatory, but it is makruh. Evidence: (1) In this ayah: 'And remember Allah during the appointed days. (Surah al-Baqarah 2:203) (2) From this ayah it is known that leaving on the 12th to Mecca is fine, and delaying is also fine. (3) The indication of this hadith shows that the Prophet performed ramy on the 13th. From Ibn Umar: 'He used to come to the jamarat on the three days after the day of Nahr, walking going and returning, and he reported that the Prophet used to do that.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Rami al-Jimar, p. 287 no. 1969) In this hadith, Ibn Umar would walk to the jamarat on the three days after the day of Nahr, i.e., up to the 13th, and said the Prophet did so, indicating that the Prophet stayed in Mina until the fourth day and performed ramy.

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling regarding leaving Mina on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah. The author states that it is sunnah to hasten the departure before sunset if one intends to leave. However, if one stays until sunset, there is no penalty (no wajib), but it is makruh (disliked). The evidence includes the Quranic verse (2:203) which allows leaving after two days (the 12th) without sin, and a hadith of Ibn Umar showing that the Prophet sometimes stayed until the 13th and performed ramy, indicating that staying is also permissible but the better act is to leave before sunset on the 12th.

Key Terms
نفر (nafr): Departure from Mina after completing the ramy (stoning).
مكروه (makruh): Disliked but not sinful; here it is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked).

Staying in Mina Until Fajr of the 13th: Ramy Becomes Wajib
Ruling that staying until Fajr of the 13th necessitates ramy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that triggers the wajib of ramy on the 13th and explain the evidence from Ibn Umar's statement.

Core Idea
Presence in Mina at Fajr of the 13th makes ramy wajib — you cannot leave without it.

This lesson addresses a specific timing rule in Hajj: when exactly does ramy of the 13th become obligatory? The text uses a companion's saying to establish that remaining until dawn binds the pilgrim to perform the stoning. We will explore the ruling, its evidence, and the practical implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ramy (stoning) on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah. The ruling: it becomes wajib if one stays in Mina until Fajr of that day.
Ramy is already sunnah on other days but on the 13th it becomes wajib under this condition.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a statement of Ibn Umar (a Qawl Sahabi). The text quotes: 'Whoever has the sun set upon him while in Mina during the middle days of Tashreeq should not depart until he stones the jamarat the next day.'
This hadith is recorded in Sunan al-Bayhaqi (or similar).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Ibn Umar's statement implies that if one stays until sunset, ramy is necessary. The Hanafi ruling extends this to Fajr: if dawn breaks, the obligation is triggered, as the time for ramy has begun.
The Hanafi school uses the companion's statement as a basis, inferring that presence at the beginning of the day (Fajr) makes ramy binding.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Other schools may set the threshold at sunset of the 13th, whereas the Hanafi school takes Fajr. This difference in timing leads to different obligations.
The cross-madhhab ikhtilaf is acknowledged but the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Once Fajr of the 13th breaks, the pilgrim must perform ramy. Leaving Mina without doing so is a sin and requires dam (sacrifice) as compensation.
The ramy of the 13th is wajib; missing it intentionally without a valid excuse necessitates dam.

Source Text

Actually, the text says: if Fajr of the 13th breaks, then ramy becomes obligatory.

Commentary
This passage explains the consequence of staying in Mina until the dawn of the 13th (the fourth day after the 10th). If one is still in Mina at Fajr of the 13th, then the ramy (stoning) of the 13th becomes obligatory (wajib). One cannot leave without performing it. The evidence is a statement of Ibn Umar that if the sun sets on the 13th (i.e., he delays), he must stay and stone the next day. This establishes that staying until Fajr makes the ramy binding.

Key Terms

اليوم الرابع (al-yawm al-rabi'): The fourth day after the day of Nahr, i.e., the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
فَجر (fajr): Dawn, the moment that triggers the obligation of ramy on the 13th.

Stopping at Muhassab after Leaving Mina is Sunnah
Establishes sunnah of alighting at Muhassab after departing Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stopping at Muhassab and identify the basis for its sunnah status.

Core Idea
Stopping at Muhassab after Mina is a confirmed sunnah, not wajib, based on the Prophet's action.

After completing the final ramy at Mina, pilgrims proceed to Mecca. The Hanafi school teaches that it is sunnah to stop briefly at a valley called Muhassab along the way. This lesson clarifies the ruling and the evidence from the Prophet's practice, helping you distinguish sunnah from obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the act mentioned: alighting at al-Muhassab after leaving Mina. Note the ruling: it is classified as a sunnah, not an obligation.
The text opens with 'And from the sunnah...' directly stating the category.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Identify the proof cited: the Prophet's own action of camping at Muhassab, linked to the historical incident of disbelievers conspiring.
The text mentions a saying of the Prophet but details are truncated; the key is that the Prophet’s practice is the proof.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the Prophet's action indicates sunnah: his consistent practice and explicit statement (if available) show it is recommended, not obligatory.
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's habitual action (fi‘l) indicates sunnah unless there is evidence of obligation.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
Recognize that other schools may differ on the strength of this act (e.g., mustahabb vs. sunnah). The Hanafi classification as sunnah muakkadah is a specific tarjih.
Disagreement does not affect the validity of Hajj; it only concerns reward.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a pilgrim should plan to stop at Muhassab for a short while after the 13th ramy. If one omits it, the Hajj is still valid but a sunnah is missed.
No compensation (dam) is required for leaving a sunnah.

Rulings on Leaving Mina on the 12th and 13th of Dhul-Hijjah
Rulings on hastening departure and staying in Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hastening departure (nafr) from Mina on the 12th and staying until the 13th, and apply the proof from Quran and Hadith.

Core Idea
Hastening departure before sunset on the 12th is sunnah; staying until sunset is makruh (no penalty); staying until Fajr of 13th makes stoning wajib.

This lesson covers the rulings on when a pilgrim may leave Mina after the days of Tashriq. Based on the Quran and the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, the Hanafi school distinguishes between hastening (recommended), delaying without penalty (disliked), and staying until the obligation of stoning becomes binding. Understanding these gradations helps the pilgrim fulfill the rites correctly without unnecessary burden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage presents three scenarios: leaving before sunset on the 12th, staying until sunset, and staying until Fajr of the 13th. Identify each and note the ruling mentioned.
2
Determine the hukm for each scenario
For each scenario, classify the ruling as sunnah (hastening), makruh tanzih (staying until sunset without penalty), or wajib (staying until Fajr makes stoning necessary).
Makruh tanzih means disliked but not prohibited; no compensation required.
3
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse (2:203) grants permission to leave after two days or stay, indicating no sin for either. The hadith of Ibn Umar shows the Prophet (ﷺ) stayed and stoned on the 13th, illustrating the recommended practice.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud; its chain is zanni al-thubut.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The verse's phrase 'no sin upon him' for both hastening and delaying shows both are permissible; the hadith's indication of staying and stoning on the 13th shows it is sunnah, but not obligatory until Fajr.
The Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub? Here the Prophet's action is indicative of sunnah, not obligation.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that staying until sunset on the 12th without a valid excuse requires a dam (penalty). Hanafi considers it only makruh, citing the verse's explicit absence of sin.
The practical difference: no penalty in Hanafi; potential dam in other schools.

سنن الحج
وهى ثالثة خُطَبِ الحج (۱۲۸۲) وتعجيل النفر اذا اراده من منى قبل غروب الشمس من اليوم الثاني عشر وان اقام بها حتى غربت الشمس من اليوم الثانى عشر فلا شيء عليه وقد اساء(۱۲۸۳) وان اقام بمنى الى طلوع فجر اليوم الرابع لزمه رميه.
بارہویں کا سورج غروب ہو گیا تو بھی کچھ واجب نہیں لیکن ایسا کرنا برا ہے۔ تشریح : ۲ رذی الحجہ کومٹی سے نکلنے کا ارادہ ہو تو سورج غروب ہونے سے پہلے نکلنا سنت ہے لیکن اگر سورج ڈوب گیا تب بھی کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہوگی ، البتہ مکروہ ہے۔
وجه : (۱) اس آیت میں ہے۔ واذكروا الله في ايام معدودات فمن تعجل في يومين فلا اثم عليه ومن تأخر فلا اثم عليه لمن اتقى. (آیت ۲۰۳ سورة البقرة (۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو دن یعنی بارہویں تاریخ کو مکہ مکرمہ آئے تب بھی کوئی بات نہیں ہے، اور اگر اس کے بعد آئے تب بھی کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث کے اشارے سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ حضور ۱۳/ تاریخ کور می کی ہے۔ . عن ابن عمر أنه كان يأتى الجمار في الايام الثلاثة بعد يوم النحر ما شيا ذاهبا و راجعا ، و يخبر أن النبي الا الله كان يفعل ذالك (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی رمی الجمارص ۲۸۷، نمبر ۱۹۶۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ابن عمر یوم النحر کے بعد تین دن تک یعنی تیرہویں تاریخ تک چل کر جمرات پر آتے تھے اور یہ بھی فرماتے کہ حضور
بھی ایسا کرتے تھے، جس کے اشارے سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور چوتھے دن بھی منی میں رہے اور رمی کی ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۲۸۳) اور اگرمنی میں چوتھے (۱۳ار تاریخ کے ) دن کی فجر طلوع ہو گئی تو اس دن کی رمی لازم ہو گئی۔
تشریح : اگر ۱۳ ذی الحجہ کی فجر طلوع ہو گئی تو اب رمی کا وقت آگیا اس لئے اب اس کو چھوڑ کر جانا جائز نہیں ہے وجه : (۱) اس قول صحابی میں ہے ۔ عن ابن عمر كان يقول من غربت عليه الشمس وهو بمنى اوسط ايام التشريق فلا ينفرن حتى يرمي الجمار من الغد. (سن المعنى ، باب من غربت له الشمس يوم النظر الاول بمنی حتی برمی الجمار یوم الثالث بعد الزوال ج خامس ص ۲۴۸، نمبر ۶ ۹۶۸) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ تیرہویں ذی الحجہ کو سورج غروب ہو جائے تو منی سے نہ چلے۔
Sunnahs of Hajj. And they are three [matters] of Hajj (1282): Hastening departure when he wants it from Mina before sunset on the twelfth day. And if he stays there until the sun sets on the twelfth day, nothing is upon him, although he has done wrong (1283). And if he stays in Mina until the dawn of the fourth day, stoning becomes obligatory upon him.
[Urdu: If the sun of the twelfth has set, still nothing is obligatory, but doing so is bad. Explanation: On the 12th of Dhul-Hijjah, if one intends to leave Mina, it is sunnah to leave before sunset. But if the sun has set, there is no harm, nothing becomes obligatory; however, it is makruh.
Proof: (1) In this verse: 'And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days. Then whoever hastens [his departure] in two days, there is no sin upon him; and whoever delays [until after the two days], there is no sin upon him for him who fears Allah.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:203). From this verse it is understood that coming to Makkah on the twelfth day is fine, and if one comes after that, there is no harm. (2) From the indication of this hadith it is understood that the Prophet (ﷺ) stayed in Mina on the 13th. ... 'From Ibn 'Umar that he used to come to the jamarat on the three days after the Day of Sacrifice, walking both going and returning, and he informed that the Prophet (ﷺ) used to do that.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Ramy al-Jimar, p.287, no.1969). In this hadith, Ibn 'Umar used to come to the jamarat walking for three days after the Day of Sacrifice, i.e., until the 13th, and he also said that the Prophet (ﷺ) used to do that. From its indication it is understood that the Prophet (ﷺ) stayed in Mina on the fourth day and performed rami.
Translation: (1283) And if the dawn of the fourth day (13th) rises upon him in Mina, then rami of that day becomes obligatory.
Explanation: If the dawn of 13th Dhul-Hijjah rises, then the time for rami has come, so it is not permissible to leave without it. Proof: (1) In this saying of a Companion: 'From Ibn 'Umar, he used to say: Whoever the sun sets upon while he is in Mina on the middle days of Tashriq, let him not depart until he ston the jamarat the next day.' (Sunan al-Ma'na? Bab...). This saying of the Companion indicates that if the sun sets on the 13th Dhul-Hijjah, one should not leave Mina.]
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage presents rulings on leaving Mina during Hajj. It is a ruling with proof type. The text begins by stating the sunnah of hastening departure before sunset on the 12th of Dhul-Hijjah. This is a recommended act (sunnah). If one remains until after sunset, no penalty (dam) is required, but it is considered makruh tanzih (disliked). Then, if one stays until the dawn of the 13th, stoning (rami) becomes obligatory (wajib) for that day. The proofs provided include the Quranic verse (2:203) which permits leaving in two days (12th) or delaying further, and hadith from Ibn 'Umar showing the Prophet (ﷺ) stayed and stoned on the 13th. The Hanafi position is that staying until after sunset on the 12th is not a violation but is disliked; staying until Fajr of the 13th makes rami wajib. This is based on the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
نفر (nafr): Departure from Mina to Makkah after the days of Tashriq.
رمي (ramy): Stoning of the jamarat by throwing pebbles.
مکروہ (makruh): A legally disliked act that is not prohibited; avoidance is rewarded.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act whose omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the Hajj.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah muakkadah): An emphasized sunnah; the Prophet regularly performed it and encouraged it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a pilgrim remains in Mina until after sunset on the 12th of Dhul-Hijjah?
A) He must sacrifice a dam.
B) Nothing is required, but it is makruh.
C) His Hajj is invalid.
D) He must stay until the 13th.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, hastening departure from Mina before sunset on the 12th is sunnah; delaying until sunset is makruh without penalty; staying until Fajr of the 13th makes stoning wajib.

Sunnah of Descending at al-Muhassab
Ruling on stopping at al-Muhassab after leaving Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on descending at al-Muhassab and identify the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Halting at al-Muhassab after Mina is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation.

This lesson examines the sunnah of al-Muhassab, a place between Mina and Makkah. The Hanafi school classifies this act as a confirmed sunnah based on the Prophet's consistent practice and explicit instruction. Understanding the distinction between sunnah and wajib is crucial for proper hajj performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is descending (nuzul) at al-Muhassab after completing the rites of Mina and before entering Makkah for tawaf. The Hanafi ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
It is not wajib, so omitting it does not require any compensation.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The primary evidence is the hadith of Anas ibn Malik, where the Prophet prayed and rested at al-Muhassab, and the hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet explicitly announced their descent there. These narrations are found in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim.
The multiple chains make the hadith mutawatir in meaning, giving it strong probative force.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
The Prophet's action (fi'l) is a source of sunnah in Hanafi usul. His statement 'We are descending tomorrow' confirms the desirability. The historical reason (showing gratitude for Islam's triumph) also underscores its merit.
Hanafi usul holds that the Prophet's consistent action indicates sunnah unless there is evidence of obligation.
4
Consider the khilaf (difference of opinion)
Some later scholars consider it merely mustahabb (recommended) rather than sunnah muakkadah, but the Hanafi school maintains the higher classification due to the strength of the evidence.
The practical difference is negligible; both encourage the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۲۸۴) منی سے نکلنے کے بعد تھوڑی دیر مقام محصب میں اترنا سنت ہے۔ تشریح : مقام محصب منی اور مکہ مکرمہ کے درمیان ہے، اس لئے جب آخری رمی کر کے منی سے مکہ مکرمہ جائے تو پہلے مصب میں ٹھہرے پھر بیت اللہ جائے یہ سنت ہے۔ وجه : (۱) آپ نے فرمایا کہ اس مقام پر کافروں نے مل کر فیصلہ کیا تھا کہ اسلام مٹادیں گے اس لئے اس مقام پر پڑاؤ ڈال کر
جتلائیں گے کہ اسلام پھل پھول کر مکہ میں واپس آگیا، اسی شکرانہ میں آپ اور صحابہ مقام محصب میں قیام پذیر ہوئے (۲) ان انس بن مالك حدثه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم انه صلى الظهر والعصر والمغرب والعشاء ورقد رقدة بالمحصب ثم ركب الی البیت فطاف به ( بخاری شریف، باب من صلى العصر يوم النفر بالا صبح ص ۲۳۷ نمبر ۱۷۶۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب نزول المحصب يوم الحفر وصلوة الظهر و ما بعدها به ص ۴۲۲ نمبر ۳۱۶۶/۱۳۰۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ منی سے نکلنے کے بعد مقام محصب
میں ٹھہر نا چاہئے ۔(۲)حدثنا ابو هريرة قال لنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم و نحن بمنی : نازلون غدا بخیف بنی حيـث تـقـاسـمـوا عـلـى الكفر . و ذالک ان قريشا و بني كنانة حالفت على بني هاشم و بنى المطلب أن لا يناكحوهم و لا يبايعوهم حتى يسلموا اليهم رسول الله الا الله یعنی بذالک ، المحصب ۔(مسلم شریف، باب استخباب نزول الحصب يوم النظر ص ۴۲۲۲ نمبر ۳۱۷۵/۱۳۱۴ / بخاری شریف، باب نزول بذی طوی قبل ان يدخل مکتہ ص ۲۳۷، نمبر ۱۷۶۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ محصب میں اس لئے ٹھہرے کہ کفار مکہ نے اس جگہ بنو ہاشم سے قطع تعلق پر اور کفر پر قسم کھائی تھی
Translation: (1284) After leaving Mina, it is sunnah to alight for a while at the place of al-Muhassab. Explanation: Al-Muhassab is located between Mina and Makkah. Therefore, when one performs the final rami and leaves Mina for Makkah, he should first halt at al-Muhassab, then go to the House (Ka'bah); this is sunnah. Proof: (1) The Prophet (ﷺ) said that at this place the disbelievers gathered together and decided to wipe out Islam, so he camped there to show that Islam had returned to Makkah flourishing. Out of gratitude, the Prophet and his Companions stayed at al-Muhassab. (2) Anas ibn Malik narrated from the Prophet (ﷺ) that he prayed Zuhr, 'Asr, Maghrib, 'Isha, and slept a short sleep at al-Muhassab, then rode to the House and performed tawaf (Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab man salla al-'Asr yawm al-nafr bil-Abtah, p.237, no.1764; Sahih Muslim, Bab istihbab nuzul al-Muhassab, p.422, no.3166/1309). From this hadith, it is understood that after leaving Mina, one should stop at al-Muhassab. (3) Abu Hurairah said: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said to us while we were in Mina: 'We are descending tomorrow at the valley of Banu Kinanah where they swore upon disbelief.' That is because the Quraysh and Banu Kinanah made an alliance against Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib not to marry them nor trade with them until they handed over the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ). That place is al-Muhassab. (Sahih Muslim, Bab istihbab nuzul al-Muhassab yawm al-nafr, p.422, no.3175/1314; Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab nuzul bi-dhi Tuwa qabl an yadkhula Makkah, p.237, no.1768). This hadith indicates that the Prophet (ﷺ) stayed at al-Muhassab because the disbelievers of Makkah had sworn at that place to sever relations with Banu Hashim and upon disbelief.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the sunnah of descending at al-Muhassab (also known as al-Abtah) after completing the rites of Mina. The author states that it is sunnah to halt there briefly before proceeding to Makkah for tawaf al-ifadah. The proofs include the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) as narrated by Anas ibn Malik, where he prayed and rested at al-Muhassab, and the historical reason for camping there: to demonstrate the triumph of Islam over the disbelievers' plot. The Hanafi school holds this as a sunnah, following the authentic hadith. It is not obligatory (wajib) but recommended.

Key Terms
محصب (Muhassab): A place between Mina and Makkah where pilgrims halt after leaving Mina before entering the city.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on descending at al-Muhassab after leaving Mina?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Mubah
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Descending at al-Muhassab after Mina is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation, and omitting it does not invalidate hajj.

Sunnahs of Zamzam Water
Rulings on drinking and using Zamzam water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah practices related to Zamzam water and identify the evidence (dalil) for each.

Core Idea
Zamzam water has specific sunnah etiquettes, and its benefit is tied to one's intention.

This passage outlines the recommended etiquettes for drinking Zamzam water and the sunnah of applying it to the body. It also highlights a unique feature: Zamzam water fulfills whatever purpose one drinks it for, based on prophetic hadiths. These actions are confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first set of sunnahs
List the etiquettes for drinking Zamzam water: facing the Qibla, mentioning Allah, breathing three times, drinking to satiation, and drinking while standing.
These are derived from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas (Ibn Majah) and the Prophet's own action (Bukhari).
2
Locate the proof for each
For facing Qibla and satiation: the instruction of Ibn 'Abbas (Ibn Majah, no.306). For standing: the hadith that the Prophet drank Zamzam while standing (Bukhari, no.1636).
The proof for breathing three times and mentioning Allah is also in the same hadith.
3
Identify the second sunnah
Pouring a little Zamzam water on the head and entire body is mentioned as a sunnah (translation 1286).
The source does not specify a separate proof for this pouring, but it is included as a general practice.
4
Understand the general virtue
The hadith 'Zamzam water is for whatever it is drunk for' (Ibn Majah, no.3062) shows that the water is beneficial according to one's intention.
This applies to worldly or religious purposes.
5
Note the sunnah of carrying it
'A'ishah's practice of carrying Zamzam water, and the Prophet (ﷺ) doing so, establishes the sunnah of taking it on journeys.
This is evidence from Tirmidhi.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه (۱۳۸۵) اور زمزم کے پانی کو خوب سیراب ہو کر ، بیت اللہ کی طرف منہ کر کے ، اس میں دیکھتے ہوئے ، کھڑے ہو کر پینا تشریح : زمزم پانی کو خوب سیراب ہو کر پئے اور بیت اللہ کی طرف دیکھتے ہوئے کھڑے ہو کر پیئے۔
وجه : (ا) كنـت عـنـد عباس جالسا فجائه رجل فقال من این جئت ؟ قال من زمزم قال فشربت منها كما ينبغي ؟ قال و كيف ؟ قال اذا شربت منها فاستقبل القبلة و اذكر اسم الله و تنفس ثلاثا و تضلع منها فاذا فرغت فاحمد الله عز و جل فان رسول الله قال ان آية ما بيننا و بين المنافقين انهم لا يتضلعون من زمزم. ( ابن ماجہ شریف ، ص ۴۴۳، نمبر ۳۰۶) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ خوب سیراب ہو کر پیو۔ اور قبلہ کا استقبال کرتے ہوئے پیو۔ (۲) اور کھڑے ہو کر پٹے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ ان ابن عباس حدثه قال سقیت رسول الله الله من زمزم فشرب و هو قائم ( بخاری شریف، باب ماجاء فی زمزم، ص ۲۶۵، نمبر ۱۶۳۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ زمزم پانی کھڑا ہو کر پئے۔
ترجمه : (۱۲۸۶) اور ماء زمزم تھوڑ اسا اپنے سر اور جسم پر ڈالنا۔ اور زمزم دنیا و آخرت کے جس مقصد کے لئے پیا جائے مفید ہے وجه : (1) جس مقصد کے لئے ماء زمزم اس کے لئے مفید ہے اس حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعـت جـابـر بـن عبد الله يقول سمعت رسول الله الا الله يقول ماء زمزم لما شرب له ابن ماجہ شریف ، ص ۴۴۳، نمبر ۳۰۶۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جس مقصد کے لئے پیا جائے وہ پورا ہوگا ۔ (۲) اور ساتھ لیجائے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة انها كانت تحمل من ماء زمزم و تخبر ان رسول الله الا الله كان يحمله - ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی حمل ماء زمزم ،ص ۲۳۵
Translation (1285): And drinking Zamzam water to satiation, facing the House of Allah, looking at it, while standing. Explanation: Drink Zamzam water to satiation, and drink while facing the Qibla and standing. Proof: (1) 'I was sitting with Ibn 'Abbas when a man came to him. He asked, 'Where have you come from?' He said, 'From Zamzam.' He said, 'Did you drink from it as it should be?' He said, 'How?' He said, 'When you drink from it, face the Qibla, mention Allah's name, breathe three times, and drink to satiation. When you finish, praise Allah Almighty. Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'The sign between us and the hypocrites is that they do not drink to satiation from Zamzam.'' (Ibn Majah, p.443, no.306). This saying of the Companion indicates to drink to satiation and while facing the Qibla. (2) And for drinking while standing, this hadith: 'Ibn 'Abbas narrated that he gave the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) water from Zamzam and he drank while standing.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab ma ja'a fi Zamzam, p.265, no.1636). This hadith shows that the Prophet drank Zamzam while standing.
Translation (1286): And pouring a little Zamzam water on his head and entire body. And Zamzam is beneficial for whatever worldly or religious purpose one drinks it for. Proof: (1) 'I heard Jabir ibn 'Abdullah say: I heard the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) say: 'Zamzam water is for whatever it is drunk for.' (Ibn Majah, p.443, no.3062). This hadith indicates that whatever purpose one drinks it for, it will be fulfilled. (2) And for taking it along [on journey], this hadith: 'From 'A'ishah that she used to carry Zamzam water and informed that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) used to carry it.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi haml ma' Zamzam, p.235).
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents two sunnahs related to Zamzam water. The first (1285) concerns the etiquettes of drinking: one should face the Qibla, mention Allah, breathe three times, drink to satiation, and drink standing. The proof includes a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas instructing these etiquettes and the Prophet's own action. The second (1286) mentions pouring a little Zamzam on one's head and body, and affirms that Zamzam water is beneficial for whatever intention one drinks it for, based on the hadith 'Zamzam is for what it is drunk for.' It also mentions the sunnah of carrying Zamzam water for travel, as the Prophet (ﷺ) did. These are recommended practices (sunnah).

Key Terms
زمزم (Zamzam): The sacred well in Makkah near the Ka'bah.
تضلع (tadallu'): Drinking to complete satiation, filling the stomach.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Facing the Qibla
B) Drinking while seated
C) Breathing three times
D) Drinking to satiation

Key Takeaway
The sunnahs of Zamzam water are confirmed by prophetic practice, and its virtue lies in the intention of the drinker.

The Sunnah of Iltizam at the Multazam
Describes the sunnah of clinging to the multazam, kissing the threshold, and touching the Kiswa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the three actions of iltizam and explain why it is considered a sunnah muakkadah based on the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Clinging to the multazam is a confirmed sunnah, proven by the Prophet's own action.

Iltizam is a beloved practice performed by the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions near the Kaaba. This lesson explains its location, the recommended actions, and the evidence that establishes it as a sunnah in the Hanafi school, helping you perform this act with confidence and understanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the passage to find what iltizam involves (placing chest/face on the multazam, clinging to the Kiswa, kissing the threshold) and note that it is explicitly called 'min al-sunnah' (from the sunnah).
The term 'sunnah' here indicates a confirmed sunnah (muakkadah) in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites a hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb describing Ibn 'Umar's action and his statement 'Thus I saw the Messenger of Allah do.' Identify which books of hadith are referenced (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah).
The hadith is a sound report, though not mutawatir; its chain is acceptable for establishing a sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action (fi'l) is the basis. In Hanafi usul, a consistent prophetic action indicates sunnah. The companion's explicit attribution ('haka ra'aytu') reinforces that this was his established practice.
No verbal command is required; the action itself demonstrates the sunnah.

And from the sunnah is clinging to the multazam, which is that he places his chest and face upon it, and clinging to the covers for a while supplicating as he wishes, and kissing the threshold of the House. Explanation: The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba is called multazam. The word multazam means to cling, because one clings there. It is mustahabb that when one intends to return to one's homeland, he comes to the multazam, places his chest and face on it, clings to the curtain of the Kaaba for a while, weeps, and supplicates for a beloved thing. Proof: (1) The hadith is this: from 'Amr bin Shu'ayb from his father, he said: I performed tawaf with 'Abdullah (Ibn 'Umar). When we came to the back of the Kaaba, I said, 'Do you not seek refuge?' He said, 'We seek refuge with Allah from the Fire.' Then he proceeded until he touched the Black Stone and stood between the corner and the door. He placed his chest, face, forearms, and palms like this, and spread them out fully, then said, 'Thus I saw the Messenger of Allah (SAW) do.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Multazam, p. 276, no. 1899; Ibn Majah, Bab al-Multazam, p. 429, no. 2962). In this hadith, the Prophet placed his chest and face on the multazam and spread his hands. Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Sunan al-Hajj section, listing recommended acts of Hajj. The first ruling is the sunnah of iltizam at the multazam. The multazam is the area between the Black Stone and the Kaaba's door. The author states that it is sunnah to press one's chest and face against it, cling to the Kiswa (covering) for a short while making supplication, and kiss the threshold of the Kaaba. The commentary adds that this is mustahabb particularly when one is about to leave Mecca, and one should weep and ask for one's greatest desire. The proof is a hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb describing that 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar placed his chest, face, arms, and palms on that spot and said he saw the Prophet (SAW) do so. This establishes the act as a confirmed sunnah. Note that in the Hanafi school, such acts are sunnah (recommended), not wajib. The hadith is from Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah.

Key Terms
الملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba where one clings to the wall.
الاستار (al-istar): The plural of sitr, meaning the curtain/covering of the Kaaba (Kiswa).
عتبة ('atabah): The threshold of the Kaaba door.

The Sunnah of Entering the Kaaba with Reverence
Ruling with proof: sunnah of entering Kaaba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering the Kaaba and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice (fi'l) that establishes it as sunnah.

Core Idea
Entering the Kaaba with reverence and praying inside is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation — the Prophet's action is the proof.

This passage addresses the etiquette of entering the Kaaba itself, a great honor for pilgrims. The author states that entering with adab and ta'dhim is sunnah, using the hadith of Ibn 'Umar as evidence. Understanding how the Prophet's specific actions (fi'l) define sunnah rulings is a key skill in Hanafi fiqh. In this lesson, we will analyze the hadith and the ruling derived from it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? Entering the Kaaba. What is the ruling according to the Hanafi school? It is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed recommendation).
The ruling is not wajib or fard, but a recommended act of virtue.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar (RA) describing that the Prophet (SAW) entered the Kaaba with companions, closed the door, and prayed inside. This is the primary proof.
The hadith is in Bukhari and Muslim, making it authentic.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith establish the ruling? The Prophet's actual practice (fi'l) demonstrates the act is permissible and recommended. The specific arrangement of pillars shows how to pray inside, but the key point is that the Prophet did it, making it a sunnah.
In Hanafi usul, fi'l al-nabi indicates mubah (permissible) or sunnah unless there is evidence of obligation.
4
Confirm the Hanafi classification
Why is it sunnah muakkadah and not just mustahabb? Because the Prophet performed this act in a sacred context with specific care, and the Companions followed, showing emphasis.
The Hanafi school relies on the consistency and context of the Prophet's actions.
5
Note the cross-madhhab agreement
All major Sunni schools (Hanafi, Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) consider entering the Kaaba and praying inside as a recommended act. There is no dispute on the ruling itself.
This is a case of muttafaq alayh (agreed upon).

The proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar describing the Prophet's entrance with several companions. In the Hanafi school, this is a sunnah, not a wajib. The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.

Visiting the Prophet's Grave After Hajj: Ruling and Recommended Practice
Ruling on visiting Madinah after Hajj with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on visiting the Prophet's grave after Hajj and identify the recommended manner of exiting Makkah for that purpose.

Core Idea
Visiting the Prophet's grave after Hajj is a sunnah muakkadah, performed by exiting Makkah from Bab Sabika and Thaniyya al-Sufla.

After completing the rituals of Hajj, the greatest remaining act of worship is to visit the Prophet (peace be upon him) in Madinah. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on this visit and the specific manner of leaving Makkah as practiced by the Prophet himself. Understanding this distinction ensures you honor a highly recommended practice without regarding it as obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is visiting the Prophet's grave after Hajj. Determine its legal classification: is it wajib, sunnah, or mubah? The author calls it 'the greatest of acts of worship', indicating high virtue.
In Hanafi fiqh, the ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah), not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited for the recommended manner of exiting Makkah. The author quotes a hadith from Ibn Umar in Sunan al-Nasa'i about the Prophet's entry and exit routes.
The hadith shows the Prophet exited from Thaniyya al-Sufla; this is the basis for the recommended practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's action (exiting from Thaniyya al-Sufla) is taken as a sunnah to be followed when leaving Makkah for Madinah, not as an obligation.
The Hanafi principle: a prophetic deed without a commanding tone indicates recommendation (sunnah), not obligation (wajib).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the disagreement: some scholars consider visiting the Prophet's grave wajib. The Hanafi school holds it as sunnah muakkadah. Understand the basis for each view.
The ikhtilaf arises from different interpretations of the evidence; both positions are respected.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
State the operative ruling for fatwa. In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that visiting the Prophet's grave is sunnah muakkadah, and exiting from Bab Sabika via Thaniyya al-Sufla is the recommended method.
This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Hanafi usul principle that actions are interpreted as recommendation unless a command indicates obligation.

Then nothing remains for him except the greatest of acts of worship, which is visiting the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions. The proof is a hadith from Nasa'i showing the Prophet's practice.

باب سبيكة (bab sabika): A gate in Makkah, the exit point towards Thaniyya al-Sufla.

Key Takeaway
Visiting the Prophet's grave after Hajj is a sunnah muakkadah, not wajib, and the recommended exit from Makkah is through Bab Sabika and Thaniyya al-Sufla.

Sunnahs of Hajj: Key Recommended Acts
List of recommended acts during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi classification of the listed acts as sunnah and identify their practice during tawaf and sa'y.

Core Idea
These acts are sunnah, not wajib; performing them earns reward, omitting them does not invalidate the Hajj.

This lesson presents a summary of some sunnah acts of Hajj as compiled by the author. In the Hanafi school, acts of Hajj are categorized into fard, wajib, sunnah, and mustahabb. The following are sunnah—recommended practices that the Prophet (peace be upon him) regularly performed. Understanding their status is crucial for correct worship, as missing a sunnah is not sinful but loses merit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that the passage lists sunnah acts, not fard or wajib. They are recommended (mustahabb) and are not required for the validity of Hajj.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between fard (obligatory), wajib (necessary), and sunnah (recommended).
2
Group by context
Note that some acts relate to entering ihram (ghusl, wudu, perfume), others to tawaf (idtiba', ramal), and sa'y (running between green pillars). This helps in practical memorization.
These contexts correspond to different phases of Hajj.
3
Note gender-specific rulings
Idtiba' (exposing right shoulder) and ramal (brisk walking) in tawaf, and running between the two green markers during sa'y, are only for men. Women do not perform these.
This is based on hadith and ruling of the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the legal consequence
Omitting a sunnah does not invalidate Hajj, but it may be considered makruh tanzihi (disliked) if habitually left. No compensation (dam or qada) is required.
This contrasts with leaving a wajib, which requires dam (sacrifice).
5
Memorize for practice
Use this list as a quick reference to remember the sunnah acts when performing Hajj. Integrate them into your practice to maximize reward.
The author mentions 'sixty sunnahs,' but only a few are listed due to OCR issues. This lesson covers the sunnahs present in the text.

.... اور جنت ، ونیکوں کی صحبت کا سوال کرنا۔
.... اور جہنم سے پناہ مانگنا۔
۲۰
...... مکہ میں داخلہ کے لئے غسل کرنا۔
..... دن میں باب معلیٰ سے مکہ میں داخل ہونا۔

..... اس طواف میں اضطباع ورمل کرنا جس کے بعد حج کے مہینے میں سعی کرنی ہو مرد کے لئے میلین اخضرین کے درمیان دوڑ نا اور باقی سعی میں آہستہ چلنا۔
سنن الحج
Thamarat al-Najah vol. 2
Sixty Sunnahs of Hajj at a Glance
337
Among the Sunnahs of Hajj: bathing (ghusl) even for a menstruating or postpartum woman, or performing ablution (wudu) at the time of ihram; wearing an izaar and rida that are new and white; applying perfume; ... praying two rak'ats after ihram; reciting talbiyah frequently after ihram; raising the voice in talbiyah when praying (for men), ... or when ascending, or when descending, or meeting a rider, and in the morning; ... and whenever he recites talbiyah, he should recite it repeatedly ... and sending blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) ... and asking for Paradise and the company of the righteous ... and seeking refuge from Hell. 20 ... bathing for entering Makkah; ... entering Makkah during the day from Bab Mu'alla; ... reciting takbir and la ilaha illa Allah when meeting (visiting) the House of Allah; ... supplicating for a beloved thing upon seeing the House of Allah, for supplication is accepted at that time; performing Tawaf al-Qudum even if it is not the months of Hajj; ... performing Idtiba' and Ramal in that tawaf, and then running between the two green pillars (for men) and walking slowly in the rest of the sa'y. Sunnahs of Hajj.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement listing some of the sixty sunnahs (recommended acts) of Hajj as summarized by the author. The list includes: performing ghusl or wudu at the time of ihram, wearing new white garments, applying perfume, praying two rak'ats after ihram, reciting talbiyah frequently and raising the voice for men especially during certain conditions (e.g., when ascending, descending, meeting a rider, and in the morning), sending blessings on the Prophet, asking for Paradise and protection from Hell, performing ghusl for entering Makkah, entering Makkah during the day from Bab Mu'alla, reciting takbir and tahlil upon seeing the Ka'bah, making supplication at that time, performing Tawaf al-Qudum (arrival tawaf) even outside the Hajj months, and for men performing idtiba' (exposing the right shoulder) and ramal (brisk walking) in that tawaf, and running between the two green markers during sa'y. It is important to note that these are all sunan, meaning they are recommended but not obligatory. Omitting them does not invalidate the Hajj but may be considered makruh tanzihi (disliked).

Key Terms
اضطباع (idtiba'): To expose the right shoulder by passing the upper garment under the right arm and over the left shoulder during tawaf.
رمل (ramal): To walk briskly with short steps during the first three rounds of tawaf.
میلین اخضرین (milayn akhḍarayn): Two green pillars or markers in the sa'y area, between which men are to run.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is listed as a sunnah of Hajj according to the passage?
A) Performing Tawaf al-Wida'
B) Running between the two green pillars during sa'y
C) Reciting the Quran during tawaf
D) Shaving the head after stoning

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts of Hajj are meritorious but not mandatory; omitting them does not affect the validity of Hajj.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
Sunnahs of Ihram
List of sunnah acts for ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and describe the sunnah acts related to entering the state of ihram for Hajj.

Core Idea
Ihram begins with purification, wearing white, and constant talbiyah.

The journey of Hajj begins with entering the state of ihram. The Hanafi school enumerates several sunnah acts that prepare the pilgrim spiritually and physically. This lesson covers the recommended practices from ghusl to the frequent recitation of talbiyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify purificatory acts
Recognize that ghusl is sunnah (even for menstruating women) and wudu is an alternative. These are acts of physical preparation.
Ghusl is preferred but not mandatory; wudu suffices.
2
List clothing and fragrance
Wearing new white garments and applying perfume (avoiding scents after ihram) are sunnah to mark the sacred state.
Perfume should be applied before donning ihram garments.
3
Recite talbiyah and supplications
After the two rak'ahs of ihram, recite talbiyah loudly at specific times (after prayer, ascending, descending, meeting riders, at dawn). Also send blessings and ask for Paradise.
Talbiyah is repeated frequently; raising voice is recommended for men.

سنن الحج
60 Sunnahs of Hajj at a glance: From the sunnahs of Hajj is to perform ghusl even for a menstruating woman or one in postpartum bleeding, or wudu at the time of ihram. Wear the lower garment and upper garment that are new and white. Apply perfume. Pray two rak'ahs of ihram. Recite talbiyah frequently after ihram. Raise the voice in talbiyah when a man prays, or ascends a height, or descends, or meets a rider, and at dawn. Whenever reciting talbiyah, recite it repeatedly, and send blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), ask for Paradise and the company of the righteous, and seek refuge from Hellfire. Perform ghusl for entering Makkah. Enter Makkah during the day through Bab al-Ma'la. Recite takbir and la ilaha illallah upon seeing the House of Allah. Upon first sight of the Ka'bah, supplicate for a beloved thing, for supplication is accepted at that time. Perform tawaf al-qudum even if it is not the month of Hajj. In this tawaf, perform idtiba' and raml for men, and then between the two green markers run and in the rest of sa'i walk calmly. Perform tawaf abundantly; for the afaqi, this is more virtuous than prayer. On the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah, after zuhr prayer in Makkah, the imam delivers a sermon, and it will be one sermon without sitting in between. In it, the people are taught the rituals of Hajj. On the Day of Tarwiyah (8th), leave Makkah for Mina after sunrise and spend the night in Mina. Then on the Day of Arafah (9th), leave Mina for Arafat after sunrise. In Arafat, the imam will deliver two sermons after zawal before combining zuhr and asr with jam' taqdim, and sit between them. In both gatherings, show humility, fear, weep, and supplicate abundantly for oneself, parents, and Muslim brothers. Then leave Arafat after sunset with dignity and tranquility. In Muzdalifah, descend away from the valley near Jabal Quzah and spend the night of the 10th in Muzdalifah. And spend the nights of Mina (10th, 11th, 12th) in Mina. At the time of stoning the jamarat, keep Mina on the right and Makkah on the left. On all days, ride at the time of stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba, walk at the time of stoning the first jamrah, walk at the time of stoning the middle jamrah, and stand in the valley at the time of stoning. Stoning on the first day should be between sunrise and zawal, and on the remaining days between zawal and sunset. For one performing Hajj al-Ifrad, slaughtering a hadi is also among the sunnah. Sunnah of Hajj.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage enumerates the sixty sunnah acts of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. The list begins with acts related to ihram: ghusl (or wudu if one cannot perform ghusl), wearing white new garments, applying perfume, and praying two rak'ahs. It emphasizes reciting talbiyah frequently and raising the voice at specific times. Upon entering Makkah, ghusl is recommended, and entering during the day through Bab al-Ma'la. The first sight of the Ka'bah prompts takbir and supplication. Tawaf al-qudum is a sunnah, even outside the Hajj months, and includes idtiba' and raml for men. Sa'i between Safa and Marwa includes running between the two green markers. The passage then covers the sermon on the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah, the departure to Mina on the 8th (Yawm al-Tarwiyah), and to Arafat on the 9th. In Arafat, the imam delivers two sermons before combining prayers, with emphasis on humility and supplication. After sunset, the pilgrims move to Muzdalifah with dignity, spend the night, and then proceed to Mina for the days of stoning. The description includes specific postures during stoning and timing. Finally, slaughtering a hadi for the one performing Hajj al-Ifrad is sunnah. All these acts are recommended but not obligatory; omitting them does not invalidate the Hajj but loses reward.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The recitation 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' which is a sunnah to recite frequently after ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when should a man raise his voice in talbiyah?
A) Only during prayer
B) When ascending a height, descending, meeting a rider, at dawn, and after prayer
C) Only at dawn
D) Only when entering the Haram

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts of ihram include purification, white garments, perfume, two rak'ahs, and frequent talbiyah, all of which enhance the spiritual preparation for Hajj.

Sunnahs of Entering Makkah and Tawaf
List of sunnah acts for entering Makkah and tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the sunnah acts related to entering Makkah and performing tawaf.

Core Idea
Entering Makkah with purity, seeing the Ka'bah, and performing tawaf with idtiba' and raml is sunnah.

After reaching Makkah, certain sunnah acts are recommended before and during tawaf. These include performing ghusl for entry, entering through Bab al-Ma'la during the day, supplicating upon seeing the Ka'bah, and specific practices during tawaf such as idtiba' and raml for men.

Guided Path
1
Entering Makkah
Perform ghusl before entering, enter during the day through Bab al-Ma'la, and recite takbir upon seeing the House of Allah.
Entering at night or through other gates is permissible but against the sunnah.
2
First sight of Ka'bah
Upon seeing the Ka'bah, make a sincere supplication for a cherished desire, as this is a time when du'a is accepted.
The supplication may be for any lawful need; no specific formula is required.
3
Performing tawaf al-qudum
Perform tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) even if outside Hajj months. For men, perform idtiba' (exposing right shoulder) and raml (brisk walking) in the first three circuits.
If the tawaf is not followed by sa'i, raml and idtiba' are not performed.

Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage enumerates the sixty sunnah acts of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. The list begins with acts related to ihram: ghusl (or wudu if one cannot perform ghusl), wearing white new garments, applying perfume, and praying two rak'ahs. It emphasizes reciting talbiyah frequently and raising the voice at specific times. Upon entering Makkah, ghusl is recommended, and entering during the day through Bab al-Ma'la. The first sight of the Ka'bah prompts takbir and supplication. Tawaf al-qudum is a sunnah, even outside the Hajj months, and includes idtiba' and raml for men. Sa'i between Safa and Marwa includes running between the two green markers. The passage then covers the sermon on the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah, the departure to Mina on the 8th (Yawm al-Tarwiyah), and to Arafat on the 9th. In Arafat, the imam delivers two sermons before combining prayers, with emphasis on humility and supplication. After sunset, the pilgrims move to Muzdalifah with dignity, spend the night, and then proceed to Mina for the days of stoning. The description includes specific postures during stoning and timing. Finally, slaughtering a hadi for the one performing Hajj al-Ifrad is sunnah. All these acts are recommended but not obligatory; omitting them does not invalidate the Hajj but loses reward.

Key Terms
اضطباع (idtiba'): Uncovering the right shoulder by passing the upper garment under the right armpit and over the left shoulder during tawaf.
رمل (raml): Walking briskly with short steps and shoulder movements during the first three rounds of tawaf.
آفاقی (afaqi): A pilgrim who comes from outside the miqat boundaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a pilgrim do upon first seeing the Ka'bah?
A) Begin tawaf immediately
B) Supplicate for something beloved
C) Recite the entire Quran
D) Perform two rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
Sunnahs of entering Makkah include ghusl, daytime entry, supplication, and tawaf al-qudum with idtiba' and raml for men.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
Sunnahs of Sa'i, Arafat, and Muzdalifah
List of sunnah acts for sa'i, Arafat, Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah acts during sa'i, at Arafat, and during the night at Muzdalifah.

Core Idea
Running between the green markers, the Arafat sermon, and spending the night in Muzdalifah are key sunnahs.

The next major phases after tawaf are sa'i between Safa and Marwa, the standing at Arafat, and the night at Muzdalifah. Each has specific sunnah acts detailed in the Hanafi list, including running between the green markers, listening to the sermon on the 7th, and supplicating profusely at Arafat.

Guided Path
1
Sa'i between Safa and Marwa
Between the two green markers (میلین اخضرین), men should run (fast pace) and in the rest of sa'i walk calmly.
The running is only between specific points, not the entire distance.
2
Sermon on 7th of Dhul-Hijjah
The imam delivers one sermon after zuhr on the 7th, teaching the Hajj rituals.
This sermon is distinct from the Friday khutbah; it is a teaching session.
3
At Arafat on the 9th
After zawal (noon), the imam gives two sermons, then combines zuhr and asr. Pilgrims should display humility, weep, and supplicate abundantly.
The combination is jam' taqdim (early combination).

حج کی سنتوں میں سے غسل کرنا ہے چاہے حائضہ اور نفاس والی ہو ۔ یا احرام کے وقت وضو ہے اور ازار و چادر پہننا جو نئے اور سفید ہوں ۔

...... مکہ میں داخلہ کے لئے غسل کرنا۔
..... دن میں باب معلیٰ سے مکہ میں داخل ہونا۔
..... بیت اللہ کی ملاقات ( زیارت) کے وقت تکبیر، ولا الہ الا اللہ پڑھنا۔

کثرت سے طواف کرنا، آفاقی کے لئے یہ فضل نماز سے افضل ہے۔ سات ذی الحجہ کو مکہ میں نماز ظہر کے بعد (امام کے لئے ) خطبہ دینا، اور یہ ایک خطبہ ہوگا بغیر درمیان میں جلسہ کئے ہوئے۔ ..... اس میں (لوگوں) کو حج کے مناسک سکھلائے جائیں۔ ... یوم ترویہ ( ۸ / تاریخ) کو مکہ سے منی کے لئے طلوع آفتاب کے بعد نکلنا اور رات منی میں گزارنا۔
پھر یوم عرفہ (۹) کو منی سے عرفات کے لئے طلوع شمس کے بعد نکلنا۔ عرفات میں امام ظہر اور عصر کی جمع تقدیم سے پہلے زوال کے بعد دو خطبے دے گا .... اور ان کے درمیان بیٹھے۔

تمام دنوں جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کے وقت سوار ہونا، اور جمرہ اولی کے وقت پیدل چلنا، اور جمرہ وسطی کی رمی کے وقت پیدل چلنا، اور رمی کے وقت بطن وادی میں کھڑا ہونا۔
