سنن الحج
60 Sunnahs of Hajj at a glance: From the sunnahs of Hajj is to perform ghusl even for a menstruating woman or one in postpartum bleeding, or wudu at the time of ihram. Wear the lower garment and upper garment that are new and white. Apply perfume. Pray two rak'ahs of ihram. Recite talbiyah frequently after ihram. Raise the voice in talbiyah when a man prays, or ascends a height, or descends, or meets a rider, and at dawn. Whenever reciting talbiyah, recite it repeatedly, and send blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), ask for Paradise and the company of the righteous, and seek refuge from Hellfire. Perform ghusl for entering Makkah. Enter Makkah during the day through Bab al-Ma'la. Recite takbir and la ilaha illallah upon seeing the House of Allah. Upon first sight of the Ka'bah, supplicate for a beloved thing, for supplication is accepted at that time. Perform tawaf al-qudum even if it is not the month of Hajj. In this tawaf, perform idtiba' and raml for men, and then between the two green markers run and in the rest of sa'i walk calmly. Perform tawaf abundantly; for the afaqi, this is more virtuous than prayer. On the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah, after zuhr prayer in Makkah, the imam delivers a sermon, and it will be one sermon without sitting in between. In it, the people are taught the rituals of Hajj. On the Day of Tarwiyah (8th), leave Makkah for Mina after sunrise and spend the night in Mina. Then on the Day of Arafah (9th), leave Mina for Arafat after sunrise. In Arafat, the imam will deliver two sermons after zawal before combining zuhr and asr with jam' taqdim, and sit between them. In both gatherings, show humility, fear, weep, and supplicate abundantly for oneself, parents, and Muslim brothers. Then leave Arafat after sunset with dignity and tranquility. In Muzdalifah, descend away from the valley near Jabal Quzah and spend the night of the 10th in Muzdalifah. And spend the nights of Mina (10th, 11th, 12th) in Mina. At the time of stoning the jamarat, keep Mina on the right and Makkah on the left. On all days, ride at the time of stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba, walk at the time of stoning the first jamrah, walk at the time of stoning the middle jamrah, and stand in the valley at the time of stoning. Stoning on the first day should be between sunrise and zawal, and on the remaining days between zawal and sunset. For one performing Hajj al-Ifrad, slaughtering a hadi is also among the sunnah. Sunnah of Hajj.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary

It emphasizes reciting talbiyah frequently and raising the voice at specific times. Upon entering Makkah, ghusl is recommended, and entering during the day through Bab al-Ma'la. Sa'i between Safa and Marwa includes running between the two green markers. The passage then covers the sermon on the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah, the departure to Mina on the 8th (Yawm al-Tarwiyah), and to Arafat on the 9th. After sunset, the pilgrims move to Muzdalifah with dignity, spend the night, and then proceed to Mina for the days of stoning. The description includes specific postures during stoning and timing. Finally, slaughtering a hadi for the one performing Hajj al-Ifrad is sunnah. All these acts are recommended but not obligatory; omitting them does not invalidate the Hajj but loses reward.

Key Terms
میلین اخضرین (maylayn akhdarayn): The two green markers between which men run during sa'i.

Key Takeaway

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
Sunnahs of Mina and Rami
List of sunnah acts for Mina and rami

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts related to staying in Mina and performing the stoning of the jamarat.

Core Idea
Stoning with specific posture, timing, and staying nights in Mina are sunnah.

The final days of Hajj are spent in Mina, performing the stoning (rami) of the three jamarat. The Hanafi list details sunnahs about the direction to face, mode of transport, timing, and the sacrifice for the ifrad pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
Posture during stoning
Keep Mina on the right side and Makkah on the left when stoning the jamarat. Stand in the valley (batin al-wadi) during stoning.
This is for the first and middle jamrah; for Jamrat al-Aqaba, riding is sunnah.
2
Transport preference
Ride when stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba; walk when stoning the first and middle jamarah.
Walking is a sign of humility except for the last jamrah where riding is established.
3
Timing of stoning
First day (10th): between sunrise and zawal. Remaining days (11th, 12th): between zawal and sunset.
Stoning after sunset on these days is not sunnah but permissible if necessary.

جمرہ عقبہ (jamrat al-aqaba): The largest of the three stoning pillars, also known as the big jamarah.

Sunnahs of Hajj (Part 1): From Makkah to Muzdalifah
List of recommended acts for the first part of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts (sunan) from the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah through the night at Muzdalifah, and explain their timing and manner.

Core Idea
Many acts of Hajj are sunnah – omission does not invalidate Hajj but reduces its perfection.

The Hanafi school has compiled a comprehensive list of sunan (recommended acts) for Hajj. These are not obligatory but are highly meritorious. In this lesson, we focus on the sunan from the sermon on the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah through the night spent at Muzdalifah. Understanding these helps you perform Hajj in the most complete manner, following the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time
Each sunnah is tied to a specific time or stage of Hajj. For example, the sermon on the 7th, leaving for Mina on the 8th, etc.
Use the text to match each act with its designated time.
2
Note the specific conditions
Some sunan have conditions: e.g., the Imam delivers the sermon, the sermon is one without sitting, etc.
Pay attention to details like 'after Dhuhr prayer' or 'between two sermons'.
3
Recognize the purpose
These acts embody humility, gratitude, and following the Prophet. For instance, abundant tawaf is more virtuous than prayer for the Afaqi.
The virtue is not just in the action but in the intention and state of heart.
4
Differentiate sunnah from wajib
Missing a sunnah does not require a sacrifice (dam) like missing a wajib. It is makruh tanzih to omit a sunnah deliberately.
This is a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh.

حج کے مناسک سکھلائے جائیں۔ ... یوم ترویہ ( ۸ / تاریخ) کو مکہ سے منی کے لئے طلوع آفتاب کے بعد نکلنا اور رات منی میں گزارنا۔ پھر یوم عرفہ (۹) کو منی سے عرفات کے لئے طلوع شمس کے بعد نکلنا۔ عرفات میں امام ظہر اور عصر کی جمع تقدیم سے پہلے زوال کے بعد دو خطبے دے گا .... اور ان کے درمیان بیٹھے۔ 11...... ان دونوں مجموعوں میں تضرع، خشوع ، آنسو بہا کر رونا، اور اپنے لئے ، والدین کے لئے اور مسلمان بھائیوں کے لئے خوب دعا کرنا۔ پھر عرفات سے غروب کے بعد وقار اور سکون سے نکلنا۔ ۳۵ .... مزدلفہ میں بطن وادی سے ہٹ کر جبل قزح کے پاس اترنا اور دسویں شب مزدلفہ میں قیام کرنا ..... اور منی کے دنوں ( ۱۲/۱۱/۱۰) منی میں رات گذارنا ۳۸ رمی جمار کے وقت منی کو داہنی جانب اور مکہ کو بائیں جانب رکھنا ۳۹ تمام دنوں جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کے وقت سوار ہونا ، اور جمرہ اولی کے وقت پیدل چلنا ا اور جمرہ وسطی کی رمی کے وقت پیدل چلنا ..... اور رمی کے وقت بطن وادی میں کھڑا ہونا رمی کا پہلے دن طلوع شمس اور زوال کے درمیان میں ہونا .... اور باقی دنوں میں زوال اور غروب کے درمیان ہونا حج افراد کرنے والے کے لئے ہدی کا ذبح کرنا بھی سنت میں سے ہے۔ سنن الحج اور صرف اس ہدی سے اور نفل ہدی سے اور قرآن و تمتع کی قربانی سے کھانا ۴۷. اور یوم نحر کو پہلے خطبہ کی طرح خطبہ کہنا سنت ہے، ... اس میں حج کے بقیہ مناسک سکھلائے جائیں بارہ تاریخ کومٹی سے نکلنے کا ارادہ ہو تو غروب شمس سے پہلے جلدی کرنا سنت ہے ) ۵۰ منی سے نکلنے کے بعد تھوڑی دیر ( مقام ) محصب میں اتر نا سنت ہے۔ اور زمزم کے پانی کو خوب سیراب ہو کر پینا 10: ۲..... بیت اللہ کی طرف منھ کر کے، اس میں دیکھتے ہوئے پینا ۵۳..... کھڑے ہوکر پینا۔ .... اور ماء زمزم تھوڑ اسا اپنے سر اور جسم پر ڈالنا۔ : ملتزم سے چمٹنا اس طرح پر کہ اپنا سینہ اور منھ اس پر رکھے سنت ہے ۵۶ تھوڑی دیر کے لئے اپنی محبوب چیز کی دعا مانگتے ہوئے غلاف بیت اللہ کو تھامنا۔ ..... بیت اللہ کی چوکھٹ کا بوسہ دینا ۵۸۔ بیت اللہ میں ادب و عظمت سے داخل ہونا (اگر ہو سکے ) ۵۹..... زیارت مدینہ کرنا۔ ۶۰: حضور ع پر درود وسلام پڑھنا۔ سنن الحج
Performing much tawaf; for the Afaqi, this is more virtuous than prayer. On the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah in Makkah, after Dhuhr prayer, (for the Imam) to give a sermon, and it will be one sermon without sitting in between. ... In it, the people should be taught the rites of Hajj. ... On Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th date), to leave Makkah for Mina after sunrise and spend the night in Mina. Then on Yawm ‘Arafah (9th), to leave Mina for ‘Arafat after sunrise. In ‘Arafat, the Imam will deliver two sermons after zawal (noon) before combining Dhuhr and ‘Asr with jam‘ taqdim ... and sit between them. ... In these two assemblies, to show humility, reverence, shed tears, and make abundant supplication for oneself, one’s parents, and Muslim brothers. Then to leave ‘Arafat after sunset with dignity and tranquility. ... In Muzdalifah, to descend away from the valley bottom near Jabal Quzah and spend the night of the 10th in Muzdalifah ... and spend the nights of Mina days (10th, 11th, 12th) in Mina. At the time of stoning the jamarat, to keep Mina on the right and Makkah on the left. On all days, to be mounted when stoning Jamrat al-‘Aqabah, and to walk when stoning the first Jamrah, and to walk when stoning the middle Jamrah ... and to stand in the valley bottom (batn al-wadi) when stoning. The stoning on the first day should be between sunrise and zawal ... and on the remaining days between zawal and sunset. For one performing Hajj al-Ifrad, slaughtering a hady is also from the Sunnah. Sunan al-Hajj. And to eat from this hady, from nafl hady, and from the sacrifices of Qur’an and Tamattu‘. On Yawm al-Nahr, to deliver a sermon similar to the first sermon is Sunnah; ... in it, the remaining rites of Hajj should be taught. If one intends to leave Mina on the 12th, it is Sunnah to hurry before sunset. After leaving Mina, to dismount briefly in al-Muhassab is Sunnah. And to drink Zamzam water to one’s fill, facing the Kaaba and looking at it, drinking while standing ... and to pour a little Zamzam water on one’s head and body. To cling to the Multazam, such that one places one’s chest and face on it, is Sunnah. For a short while, to hold the covering of the Kaaba while supplicating for a beloved thing. To kiss the threshold of the Kaaba. To enter the Kaaba with reverence and respect (if possible). To visit Madinah. To send blessings and peace upon the Prophet (peace be upon him). Sunan al-Hajj.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a list of recommended acts (sunan) in Hajj, as compiled by the Hanafi school. These are not obligatory (wajib) but are highly meritorious and increase the reward of the pilgrimage. The list covers various stages of Hajj: abundant tawaf (circumambulation) before the days of Hajj, the sermon on the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah, the journeys to Mina and ‘Arafat, the sermons and supplications at ‘Arafat, the night at Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat (with specific postures and timings), slaughtering of hady for those performing Ifrad, eating from the sacrifices, the sermon on the Day of Nahr, early departure from Mina on the 12th, stopping at Muhassab, drinking Zamzam water with etiquettes, clinging to the Multazam, kissing the Kaaba’s threshold, entering the Kaaba, and visiting the Prophet’s mosque in Madinah. Each act is described with its specific conditions and manner. The repetition of 'Sunan al-Hajj' at the end signals that the list is complete. In the Hanafi school, these sunan are based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and are separate from the wajibat (obligatory acts) of Hajj, which are also established. The category 'sunnah' here includes both mu’akkadah (emphasized) and ghayr mu’akkadah (non-emphasized) sunan, though the text does not differentiate. Missing any of these does not require a dam (compensatory sacrifice) but reduces the perfection of the Hajj.

Key Terms
سنت (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet regularly performed; omission is disliked but not sinful in Hanafi fiqh.
آفاقی (afaqi): A pilgrim who comes from outside the Miqat boundaries, not a resident of Makkah.
خطبہ (khutbah): A sermon delivered by the Imam, containing guidance and reminders.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On which date does the Imam deliver a sermon in Makkah after Dhuhr?
A) 7th Dhul-Hijjah
B) 8th Dhul-Hijjah
C) 9th Dhul-Hijjah
D) 10th Dhul-Hijjah

Key Takeaway
The first part of the sunan of Hajj includes specific acts from the 7th to the night at Muzdalifah, all recommended but not obligatory.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
Sunnahs of Hajj (Part 2): Stoning, Sacrifice, and Final Rites
List of recommended acts for the latter part of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sunan related to stoning, hady, the sermon on Yawm al-Nahr, early departure, Muhassab, Zamzam, Multazam, and visiting Madinah.

Core Idea
Sunnan of Hajj include etiquettes of stoning, sacrifice, and visiting the Kaaba and Madinah.

After the key days, there are additional recommended acts that perfect the Hajj. These include specific postures for stoning, eating from the sacrifice, the sermon on the 10th, early departure on the 12th, stopping at Muhassab, drinking Zamzam, clinging to Multazam, kissing the threshold, entering the Kaaba, and visiting the Prophet's mosque in Madinah. Understanding these ensures one completes Hajj in the most comprehensive way.

Guided Path
1
Identify each sunnah and its context
Each act is tied to a specific place or time: e.g., stoning postures, hady for Ifrad, sermon on Yawm al-Nahr.
Match the act with its proper setting.
2
Note the manner of performance
Details like being mounted or walking, standing in the valley, etc., are important.
These etiquettes distinguish the sunnah from a mere permissible act.
3
Understand the purpose
These acts show devotion, following the Prophet’s example, and seeking blessings.
For example, drinking Zamzam with facing the Kaaba is an act of reverence.
4
Differentiate from wajib
Like part 1, these are not obligatory. Missing them does not invalidate Hajj.
Only wajib acts require dam; sunnan do not.

Performing much tawaf; for the Afaqi, this is more virtuous than prayer. On the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah in Makkah, after Dhuhr prayer, (for the Imam) to give a sermon, and it will be one sermon without sitting in between. ... In it, the people should be taught the rites of Hajj. ... On Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th date), to leave Makkah for Mina after sunrise and spend the night in Mina. Then on Yawm ‘Arafah (9th), to leave Mina for ‘Arafat after sunrise. In ‘Arafat, the Imam will deliver two sermons after zawal (noon) before combining Dhuhr and ‘Asr with jam‘ taqdim ... and sit between them. ... In these two assemblies, to show humility, reverence, shed tears, and make abundant supplication for oneself, one’s parents, and Muslim brothers. Then to leave ‘Arafat after sunset with dignity and tranquility. ... In Muzdalifah, to descend away from the valley bottom near Jabal Quzah and spend the night of the 10th in Muzdalifah ... and spend the nights of Mina days (10th, 11th, 12th) in Mina. At the time of stoning the jamarat, to keep Mina on the right and Makkah on the left. On all days, to be mounted when stoning Jamrat al-‘Aqabah, and to walk when stoning the first Jamrah, and to walk when stoning the middle Jamrah ... and to stand in the valley bottom (batn al-wadi) when stoning. The stoning on the first day should be between sunrise and zawal ... and on the remaining days between zawal and sunset. For one performing Hajj al-Ifrad, slaughtering a hady is also from the Sunnah. Sunan al-Hajj. And to eat from this hady, from nafl hady, and from the sacrifices of Qur’an and Tamattu‘. On Yawm al-Nahr, to deliver a sermon similar to the first sermon is Sunnah; ... in it, the remaining rites of Hajj should be taught. If one intends to leave Mina on the 12th, it is Sunnah to hurry before sunset. After leaving Mina, to dismount briefly in al-Muhassab is Sunnah. And to drink Zamzam water to one’s fill, facing the Kaaba and looking at it, drinking while standing ... and to pour a little Zamzam water on one’s head and body. To cling to the Multazam, such that one places one’s chest and face on it, is Sunnah. For a short while, to hold the covering of the Kaaba while supplicating for a beloved thing. To kiss the threshold of the Kaaba. To enter the Kaaba with reverence and respect (if possible). To visit Madinah. To send blessings and peace upon the Prophet (peace be upon him). Sunan al-Hajj.

Commentary
This passage is a list of recommended acts (sunan) in Hajj, as compiled by the Hanafi school. These are not obligatory (wajib) but are highly meritorious and increase the reward of the pilgrimage. The list covers various stages of Hajj: abundant tawaf (circumambulation) before the days of Hajj, the sermon on the 7th of Dhul-Hijjah, the journeys to Mina and ‘Arafat, the sermons and supplications at ‘Arafat, the night at Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat (with specific postures and timings), slaughtering of hady for those performing Ifrad, eating from the sacrifices, the sermon on the Day of Nahr, early departure from Mina on the 12th, stopping at Muhassab, drinking Zamzam water with etiquettes, clinging to the Multazam, kissing the Kaaba’s threshold, entering the Kaaba, and visiting the Prophet’s mosque in Madinah. The category 'sunnah' here includes both mu’akkadah (emphasized) and ghayr mu’akkadah (non-emphasized) sunan, though the text does not differentiate. Missing any of these does not require a dam (compensatory sacrifice) but reduces the perfection of the Hajj.

Key Terms
ہدی (hady): An animal sacrificed during Hajj, either as a required offering (for Qiran/Tamattu‘) or as a voluntary act.
رمی (rami): The act of throwing pebbles at the jamarat pillars during the days of Tashriq.
ملتزم (Multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The sunan of the latter part of Hajj include detailed etiquettes of stoning, sacrifice, and visiting the Kaaba, all recommended to perfect the pilgrimage.
